         <div id="comment-127246" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name"><a href="http://lintiwen.github.io" rel="external nofollow" class="url">tiwen</a> <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127246"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-23T20:35:05+00:00">March 23, 2016 at 8:35 pm</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>Another insane thing is NPM uses caret versions (^1.2.3) by default. Caret versioning means you’ll always get latest minor releases instead of the EXACT version when you installed it.</p> 
          <p>Using caret versioning means blindly trust any 3rd party developers are honest and will do their job right. Unfortunately, there’s one time that babel-core shipped a broken patch and the production system at my company went down for several hours. How ridiculous!</p> 
          <p>Any when I try to bring up this to our JS “programmers”, they seemed to think this is OKAY.</p> 
          <p>Back to your point,<br> YES, there are tons of NPM users who actually don’t know what programming really is.</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127246#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127246&quot;, &quot;127246&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to tiwen">Reply</a>

              <span class="name">Dustin Voss <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
              <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127398"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-24T13:56:52+00:00">March 24, 2016 at 1:56 pm</time></a> </span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
              <p>It is NOT reasonable to run Javascript on the server. It isn’t strongly typed, so you only find out about issues at run-time. It doesn’t have a robust debugger. It isn’t multi-threaded. It (and its packages) are poorly documented. The poor quality of its documentation is made worse by how the language and its so-called standard libraries are fragmented across browsers and servers. And the language itself is designed like shit.</p> 
              <p>Some of these issues are shared by other scripting languages as well, but Python and Ruby are at least well-designed and consistent.</p> 
              <p>Call me a curmudgeon if you must, but a language like C# or Swift or Dylan or even Java is simply better.</p>

             <li class="comment even depth-4" id="li-comment-127475"> <a name="comment-127475"></a> 
              <div class="comment-container"> 
               <div class="avatar">
                <img alt="" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/1c1f4389e7b60bcf562d6b1799152318?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/1c1f4389e7b60bcf562d6b1799152318?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
               </div> 
               <div id="comment-127475" class="comment-content"> 
                <span class="name">Tex <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
                <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127475"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-25T12:56:14+00:00">March 25, 2016 at 12:56 pm</time></a> </span> 
                <span class="edit"></span> 
                <p>The fact that is a dynamic language is not the problem. You’re WAY off the mark there. There are many robust dynamic languages, Python being my go to, Ruby a close second. In fact, I don’t remember the last time I’ve used a “strongly typed” language, they’re best avoided unless needed for their features. </p> 
                <p>Javascript’s problem is that it has some serious flaws in the language itself, and as everyone has pointed out, does not have an extensive core (like Python or Ruby). As a result, there is no cohesion in the community and everyone is left to run amok to do their own thing.</p> 
                <p>It’s unfair to say Javascript programmers are bad programmers, but I think the author was being a bit ironic. On the other hand, Javascript developers they are deluding themselves if they believe that it is a serious language. Many younger developers that have recently entered industry don’t remember the time when Javascript was derided, that it was a necessary evil, and adequate enough to do some things on the browser. Prototype came along to make it suck less, and jQuery emerged to make it suck even more, but these frameworks came about because Javascript just flatly sucks.</p> 
                <p>The fact that people run web servers with nodejs now is mind boggling. Javascript has made many astounding leaps in the last 15 years or so. That’s why under my watch, nodejs will never run a serious application on a server, simply because the language itself is flawed.</p> 
                <div class="reply"> 
                 <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127475#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127475&quot;, &quot;127475&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Tex">Reply</a>

              <ul class="children"> 
               <li class="comment odd alt depth-5" id="li-comment-127484"> <a name="comment-127484"></a> 
                <div class="comment-container"> 
                 <div class="avatar">
                  <img alt="" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/510793539c7f356854e7796515ab8846?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/510793539c7f356854e7796515ab8846?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
                 </div> 
                 <div id="comment-127484" class="comment-content"> 
                  <span class="name">Lord Rybec <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
                  <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127484"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-25T22:33:27+00:00">March 25, 2016 at 10:33 pm</time></a> </span> 
                  <span class="edit"></span> 
                  <p>Why do people who claim to be programmers not understand that “static typing” and “strongly typed” are two different things? Python is both dynamically typed and strongly typed. If you have been using Python recently, then you certainly should remember using a strongly typed language.</p> 
                  <p>Let me explain:</p> 
                  <p>There is statically and dynamically typed.</p> 
                  <p>Statically typed means a variable cannot change type, once it has been given a type. In C, C++, Java, and similar languages, this is done by declaring a variable to be a specific type. In Haskell, a function is typed implicitly based on its return type and how it is used.</p> 
                  <p>Dynamically typed means that the type can change. In Python, you can take a variable that currently contains a string and assign it to an integer. Most scripting languages are dynamically typed as well.</p> 
                  <p>There is also strongly and weakly typed, which are totally different from static/dynamic.</p> 
                  <p>A strongly typed language prevents variable types from being misused with other types. For example, in Python, you cannot add a string to an integer. This is what strongly typed means, and it has nothing to do with whether the variable can change types dynamically or not.</p> 
                  <p>A weakly typed language allows type misuse, often by implicit casting. PHP is a an example of a weakly typed language. JavaScript is as well. The problem with weak typing is that when you do ‘a’ + 1, you end up with ‘a1’, when you thought the variable containing the ‘a’ was an integer or the variable holding the 1 was a string, and now you have a runtime error that is extremely difficult to find.</p> 
                  <p>Research has shown that dynamically types languages (like Python) are often much faster to code in than statically typed languages (like Java), without significantly more errors (the primary argument given against dynamic typing is that it is more prone to errors, but the evidence does not support this claim). You don’t need research to see that weakly typed languages are a problem. PHP and JS, and the loads of poorly written programs that would have been saved with strong typing are evidence enough. And, if you happen to use these languages regularly, you will also be aware of the fact that weak typing make debugging take many times longer.</p> 
                  <p>The problem has nothing to do with dynamic or static typing. Dustin said that the weak typing was a problem, and it is. Weak typing has been a problem for PHP developers for decades, and it is an equally annoying problem with JS.</p> 
                  <div class="reply"> 
                  </div>
                  <!-- /.reply --> 
                 </div>

           <div id="comment-127299" class="comment-content"> 
            <span class="name">Flo <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
            <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127299"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-24T03:29:38+00:00">March 24, 2016 at 3:29 am</time></a> </span> 
            <span class="edit"></span> 
            <p>Yes, and having dozens of “crazy small” dependencies add a layer of complexity that is not “crazy small” anymore. If you had one or two library-dependencies that include much stuff (like Apache Commons in Java), ok, but bloating your project with dozens of dependencies for every little bit of code does not reduce complexity at all….</p> 
            <div class="reply"> 
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127299#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127299&quot;, &quot;127299&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Flo">Reply</a> 
            </div>
            <!-- /.reply --> 
           </div>
           <!-- /comment-content --> 
           <div class="fix"></div> 
          </div>

          <div class="fix"></div> </li>

       <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" id="li-comment-127251"> <a name="comment-127251"></a> 
        <div class="comment-container"> 
         <div class="avatar">
          <img alt="" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/9055b6c1d07708555ec584d03c387f15?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/9055b6c1d07708555ec584d03c387f15?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
         </div> 
         <div id="comment-127251" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name"><a href="http://www.catonmat.net" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Peteris Krumins</a> <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127251"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-23T20:57:22+00:00">March 23, 2016 at 8:57 pm</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>My advice to “prefer core-language solutions to small abstractions to small helper libraries to general libraries to frameworks” (<a href="http://bit.ly/1UlQzcH" rel="nofollow">http://bit.ly/1UlQzcH</a>) hasn’t been more relevant than today.</p> 
          <p>Software should be developed using least amount of complexity, dependencies, effort and using fundamental tools that have been and will be here for the next 20 years. Cut those dependencies, you don’t need them. They’re here today and won’t be here tomorrow.</p>

          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>BTW, the toString.call(…) is slow as hell, and will over many fn calls using this waste you a ton of performance.</p> 
          <p>Better to use<br> if (testvar.constructor === Array)…</p> 
          <p>Or do<br> switch (testvar.constructor) { case Array:…; case String:…; … }<br> etc.</p> 
          <p>No slow generic Class Function call, no expensive string comp, all pointer comparisons only…</p>

       <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" id="li-comment-127257"> <a name="comment-127257"></a> 
        <div class="comment-container"> 
         <div class="avatar">
          <img alt="" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a261e872301526fbca7b520817699be0?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a261e872301526fbca7b520817699be0?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
         </div> 
         <div id="comment-127257" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name">javascript <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127257"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-23T21:34:11+00:00">March 23, 2016 at 9:34 pm</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>The comments here show a real ignorance of the history of Javascript. </p> 
          <p>First thing to understand: Javascript code runs in a TON of slightly different implementations. IE8, IE9, Safari, Node, SpiderMonkey, whatever the fuck. Oftentimes this is fine and you can ignore every other implementation but the subset you care about. But sometimes you will want to reuse code across a shitton of these environments (THE SITE DOESNT WORK IN IE8 screams your boss), so you write your “5 minutes of code”, *YOU WRITE SOME TESTS*, and you test a bajillion times until your tests pass everywhere and your code is performant enough and you never have to do that again, whew. THIS IS NOT AS EASY AS IT SOUNDS.</p> 
          <p>That is what you’re seeing here. This has nothing to do with modern Node or Javascript code. `isArray` is a polyfill for Christ’s sake. No one *ever*, *ever*, *ever*, should want to rewrite polyfills, but they have their place for the sake of compatibility. Blame it on the IE8 user percentage.</p> 
          <p>So yes, Javascript, across a billion implementations and environments, can be extremely ugly. How could it not be? It is clearly getting better, and as we slowly move forward and shake old implementations, it can only improve. </p> 
          <p>Moreover I think your general point is completely wrong. Yes these are small modules, but modularizing everything is the only way to go. The other route – rewrite it in 5 minutes every time! – clearly breaks down fast. Copy and paste my code, then copy and paste the tests into the test suite (if you’re writing code without tests, you don’t get to have an opinion). But then a month later you notice a small bug in some corner case – padding a String to a negative amount goes into an infinite loop! And you fix the bug, add a test, but now you have 5 other copies to update, with no way to keep them in sync. Good luck with that. I’ll be over here, with my modules, running correct code.</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127257#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127257&quot;, &quot;127257&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to javascript">Reply</a> 
          </div>

       <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" id="li-comment-127267"> <a name="comment-127267"></a> 
        <div class="comment-container"> 
         <div class="avatar">
          <img alt="" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/527f4b1d6362511b4fae2321a1f9223f?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/527f4b1d6362511b4fae2321a1f9223f?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
         </div> 
         <div id="comment-127267" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name">Robert Fletcher <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127267"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-23T23:12:39+00:00">March 23, 2016 at 11:12 pm</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>Dealing with the deeply nested dependencies has caused us no end of frustrations. A dependency of a dependency of a dependency breaks and we’re left trying to trace the source of the error and figure out which repo to open an issue on. I don’t particularly care to have it in our codebase either, though, unless it’s something that I want to heavily modify and maintain myself. If I’m developing an application, utility libraries like underscore/lodash are a huge boon, or the likes of ActiveSupport in the ruby ecosystem. You can require in just the parts you need without having to bloat your dependency tree.</p> 
          <p>It’s a little different as a library developer than an application developer, though. I’d say if you’re a library developer, you can do your users a service by including a little of the extra utility code in your library rather than adding extra dependencies. You aren’t really saving space when you’re downloading the extra boilerplate anyway.</p> 
          <p>Mike Perham discussed this topic recently, too:<br> <a href="https://www.mikeperham.com/2016/02/09/kill-your-dependencies/" rel="nofollow">https://www.mikeperham.com/2016/02/09/kill-your-dependencies/</a></p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127267#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127267&quot;, &quot;127267&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Robert Fletcher">Reply</a>

         <div id="comment-127269" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name"><a href="http://therealmarv.com" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Marvin</a> <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127269"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-23T23:18:57+00:00">March 23, 2016 at 11:18 pm</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>I thing you are wrong. Other languages hide that sort trivial complexity you are pointing at in their Standard libraries (take e.g. Python or C++). JavaScript does not have that for whatever historic reason. The problem is more the whole npm system and how it works.<br> And beside that my main job as programmer is not to just to program… it’s most of the time not reinventing the wheel again and again. Reinventing programmers are not good programmers for me. I’m sitting on the shoulders of giants and I want to solve problems while programming… it does not mean I don’t know how certain things work.</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127269#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127269&quot;, &quot;127269&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Marvin">Reply</a>

        <ul class="children"> 
         <li class="comment even depth-2" id="li-comment-128033"> <a name="comment-128033"></a> 
          <div class="comment-container"> 
           <div class="avatar">
            <img alt="" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/39070f4d752dc965b716275da4e66b50?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/39070f4d752dc965b716275da4e66b50?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
           </div> 
           <div id="comment-128033" class="comment-content"> 
            <span class="name">pq <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
            <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-128033"><time pubdate datetime="2016-04-15T18:22:10+00:00">April 15, 2016 at 6:22 pm</time></a> </span> 
            <span class="edit"></span> 
            <p>When you have to implement some function you may either implement it yourself or look if there is an implementation by someone else that you can find and use.<br> This second process involves these steps:<br> – look for one or more libraries which implement the functionality you need<br> – investigate these libraries to see if they do what you expect and they are good enough for you to use (for example, are they being maintained? Do they depend on something else in order to work? Does the same quality standards apply to their dependencies?)<br> – add them to the project, and maintain the dependency (for example, update to new versions when needed, eventually fixing the code when the functions you were using are removed from the library or deprecated, replace the library with some other would the above condition for its inclusion become false)<br> – learn which functionality the dependency included has, so that next time i need something that is available there I won’t add yet another dependency, doing all the steps above.</p> 
            <p>If the included library is a single function with a simple algorithm which could be written in theory in about 30 secs, why people are taking the effort to even think about looking for a library? I have some theories:<br> 1) you need a lot of such small function, and you hope to find them all in a single library, or<br> 2) you are not really doing all these steps, in particular checking the quality of the library yourself but you trust the number of downloads, maybe also because<br> 3) you can’t really write that simple function, or at least not in 30 secs, and thus you can’t even understand whether the library you’re including is good quality, and your usual strategy of asking on StackOverflow for people to solve your problem will likely take longer and is better to reserve this card for your “real work”.</p> 
            <p>Some final rants:</p> 
            <p> – It is not about reinventing the wheel, the wheel is not even needed here because the objective is at 30 second walk from you. Unless you need them for your wheelchair, in that case yeh I suggest you buy them instead of trying to build them by yourself.<br> – DRY is “don’t repeat yourself”, not “don’t repeat others”. It doesn’t mean you cannot write your own code if someone else wrote it for you, it means that you should not write it more than once.<br> – To stay in topic, there is another design principle known as KISS, which you may know. Dependencies create complications, conflict, code bloat, increase the number of points of failure. Lot of small dependencies from different developers decrease overall coherency of the system, may not work nicely together (or not be tested to keep working nicely together with future updates), which is something whomever used lots of LaTeX packages in the same document know by experience. Is it better to avoid them unless necessary.</p> 
            <div class="reply"> 
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=128033#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-128033&quot;, &quot;128033&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to pq">Reply</a> 
            </div>

           </div>

         <div id="comment-127270" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name"><a href="http://nanoguy.blogspot.com" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Guy</a> <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127270"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-23T23:24:33+00:00">March 23, 2016 at 11:24 pm</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>It was a delightful experience reading all these comments and watching my internal opinion drift back and forth as each writer had their say. I want to thank the entire community for all I learned during that process. </p> 
          <p>I have to agree with many who point out that re-writing functions, especially tedious functions, is not DRY compliant. On the other hand the exercise of our art as software engineers, designers and computer scientists is often improved when we take the time to focus on the basics of what we do and take it upon ourselves to understand as well as be able to perform the steps of implementing and testing what should be easy, straight-forward tasks. It is often in remastering something we thought we already knew that new insights are generated.</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127270#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127270&quot;, &quot;127270&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Guy">Reply</a>

         <li class="comment even depth-2" id="li-comment-127418"> <a name="comment-127418"></a> 
          <div class="comment-container"> 
           <div class="avatar">
            <img alt="" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/b55b68646bfacb1b4cb2190548773d96?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/b55b68646bfacb1b4cb2190548773d96?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
           </div> 
           <div id="comment-127418" class="comment-content"> 
            <span class="name">Steve <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
            <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127418"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-24T16:56:12+00:00">March 24, 2016 at 4:56 pm</time></a> </span> 
            <span class="edit"></span> 
            <p>It really is a matter of where one chooses to ‘cut nature at the joints,’ isn’t it?</p> 
            <p>Throughout the preceding rhetoric around, ‘where did the art of programming go?’ I didn’t notice anyone argue for pushing and popping registers in assembler, or painting screens with memory-mapped displays.</p> 
            <p>It seems we are merely experiencing the next batch of growing pains, as the ‘art of programming’ shifts from inventing to re-use, from managing algorithms to managing [micro]codebases — and importantly, how to strike the balance given current realities.</p> 
            <div class="reply"> 
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127418#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127418&quot;, &quot;127418&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Steve">Reply</a>

         <div id="comment-127281" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name">Tarun Elankath <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127281"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-24T00:49:55+00:00">March 24, 2016 at 12:49 am</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>If I write my own lpad function, I then need to write unit tests for this function. lpad is only one function – there can be dozens of other such ‘micro’ functions. In the ideal world, the JS standard library would have all such frequently used functions, but it is not an ideal world. The reason for the hyper-modularization in the JS world is to avoid pulling in large modules that increase file size. It would have been so much better if all these super commonly used micro functions became part of ES7.</p>

            <div class="comment-container"> 
             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/510793539c7f356854e7796515ab8846?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/510793539c7f356854e7796515ab8846?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
             </div> 
             <div id="comment-127485" class="comment-content"> 
              <span class="name">Lord Rybec <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
              <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127485"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-25T22:49:34+00:00">March 25, 2016 at 10:49 pm</time></a> </span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
              <p>Exactly. If you are such a poor programmer that you need unit tests for a 4 line function… Honestly, I don’t know what to say.</p> 
              <p>For small functions that do trivial things, you manually test once, and then you walk away. “What if you need to change the function?” I hear. If that is the case, then it is either not trivial, or you are trying to add functionality that does not belong in that function.</p> 
              <p>I think, perhaps, part of the problem here is that people are trying to take unit testing down to a level that is way too small? Are you ever tempted to compile to assembler and make unit tests for individual lines of assembly code? (If anyone reading this just said, “Hey, good idea!” no, it is not a good idea.) Neither am I, and I’ll tell you, this is what it sounds like they are expecting.</p> 
              <p>Besides that, if it is so hard to write a unit test for a 4 line function, then perhaps you should start looking into jobs in a field that is less strenuous.</p>

I remember one time my node_modules folder was at 300K files and 1.2G size. JS is great, but npm is shit.</p>

          <p>When you’re coding, it’s often mind-bogging to leave bebind the entire big structure etc, and to focus on writing that function that does simple left-padding. I often hate it because you have to leave what you’re doing at the moment and dig down to the lowest level of details to write that left-pad function, which programmers in the world should have solved it a million times.</p>

         <li class="comment even depth-2" id="li-comment-127486"> <a name="comment-127486"></a> 
          <div class="comment-container"> 
           <div class="avatar">
            <img alt="" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/510793539c7f356854e7796515ab8846?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/510793539c7f356854e7796515ab8846?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
           </div> 
           <div id="comment-127486" class="comment-content"> 
            <span class="name">Lord Rybec <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
            <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127486"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-25T23:15:20+00:00">March 25, 2016 at 11:15 pm</time></a> </span> 
            <span class="edit"></span> 
            <p>For 11 lines, copy/paste is better! For a single small function, if its current implementation works for your project, and if you can easily tell that the code is not malicious or buggy, copy/paste it. The biggest benefit of including over pasting is that you get bug fixes with a simple update. No 11 line function should be so complicated that you cannot tell if it is buggy or not. (And if it is too complicated for you, you should consider that you might be a bad programmer.)</p> 
            <p>If you need 100 small functions, something is probably wrong, but if you insist, put them in a separate utility file and go from there.</p> 
            <div class="reply"> 
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127486#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127486&quot;, &quot;127486&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Lord Rybec">Reply</a>

       <li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="li-comment-127315"> <a name="comment-127315"></a> 
        <div class="comment-container"> 
         <div class="avatar">
          <img alt="" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/1577f0cc5490e6ccde6cc5826b2c4155?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/1577f0cc5490e6ccde6cc5826b2c4155?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
         </div> 
         <div id="comment-127315" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name">Hok Shun Poon <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127315"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-24T05:23:57+00:00">March 24, 2016 at 5:23 am</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>Programming with the Internet is a superpower.</p> 
          <p>Programmers are those who don the cape,<br> Have an ambition to build what never existed before.<br> They spread their hand and raise it to the ethers of FOSS<br> Summoning code blocks from NPM and StackOverflow<br> To assemble what they wanted to assemble at lightning speed<br> And gets a kick out of seeing their little creation spring to life.</p> 
          <p>There is no one way to do it.<br> Some might write the implementation of isArray inline a thousand times because ‘they know how to code’ (where in fact they just know how to fill the bits missing from Javascript).<br> Some might write it themselves and use that function every time.<br> Some might be using lodash anyway so they go use that.<br> Some might have better things to do than to learn about the inadequacies of Javascript, and find that grabbing the isArray dependency from NPM the way to go because it’s got the lowest conceptual gap (I don’t know how to do X… well there’s an NPM package called isArray that does X for me. I’ll grab it, problem solved). Who can honestly say they haven’t done this before?</p> 
          <p>It’s all the same —&nbsp;it’s different ways of copying and pasting strings into a code file, or into your brain, as the case may be. It’s all gibberish for the computer at the end of the day, and some approaches are better than others.</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127315#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127315&quot;, &quot;127315&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Hok Shun Poon">Reply</a>

          <p>“Do you make your own shoes? No, you buy them in a store. Most don’t care how the shoe is made. Just how good it fits.”</p> 
          <p>I can’t put it better myself. Even though something may seems so small and insignificant, a lot of work has gone into creating it.</p> 
          <p>Therefore, instead of copying it or writing your own version it is better to use modules as they can be updated once and then would work on all other packages that require it.</p>

       <li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1" id="li-comment-127331"> <a name="comment-127331"></a> 
        <div class="comment-container"> 
         <div class="avatar">
          <img alt="" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/e7cec005712fe50630175e1dc33ddadd?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/e7cec005712fe50630175e1dc33ddadd?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
         </div> 
         <div id="comment-127331" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name">Nobody <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127331"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-24T06:39:23+00:00">March 24, 2016 at 6:39 am</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>Sorry, but i also think you should be getting down off your high horse. </p> 
          <p>Programming is about creating stuff, not re-inventing the wheel 100 times. For dozens of years, developers re-implemented all their stuff (all except the standard libraries, e.g. stdc) constantly , because sharing of libraries was difficult. Now its easy. </p> 
          <p>The real issue is using javascript as programming language. Checking if an integer is greater than 0 should be written “if(var &gt; 0)”. The packages you mention, like isPositiveInteger or isArray, provide simple functionality which should already be integrated in JS itself. </p> 
          <p>You are saying “everyone can write it himself in 5 minutes of googling”, but i think you are not realizing what you are saying. Developers should copy paste code from stackoverflow? How about updates and bugfixes? Or you say “you have to write it yourself”, but just look at your examples of isPositiveInteger or isArray. Look at it very closely. This is not code which is developed, this is code which accidentally works and returns the correct result in most cases (for most JS implementations). This is not code which developer cannot and should not create by themself. </p> 
          <p>Dont get my wrong, the JS and NPM situation is a bit a mess. But your conclusion is still wrong.</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127331#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127331&quot;, &quot;127331&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Nobody">Reply</a>

          <span class="name">CarbyAu <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127335"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-24T07:00:02+00:00">March 24, 2016 at 7:00 am</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>I don’t program, but it strikes me that this is DLL HELL all over again…..</p> 
          <p>Personally, I would modular dependencies should be a considered decision.</p> 
          <p>Upside, get to reuse code (which last I heard was a good thing)<br> Downside, control over said code…</p> 
          <p>There is no right answer for all situations personally I would lean towards removing dependencies where possible.</p>

          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>The Go language (I am not fan) give error when you declare a variable -or other thing- AND YOU DO NOT USE IT AFTER.</p> 
          <p>That’s common sense, however I see maybe obfuscated code won’t work (if you use open source, why obfuscate?).</p> 
          <p>First that, and another thing: if a function or module is so popular, GitHub may implement some statistics about it for a human read it (indeed, this article is about that).</p> 
          <p>My point is: let’s incorporate that module -very popular- to the language; I call it “canonize it”.</p> 
          <p>“Canonization” will be done by hundred of eyes and garantize it works well. Of course, we must publicite the new version for everyone’s knowing: if you want continue using your own -or other- modules you are entirely free.</p> 
          <p>Final point: if you are a programmer your users will talk with you at any mistake -however they NEVER give you a congratulation when all is working fine- and the other hand they never will understand that you are using code from other programmer. You are alone in this, Google won’t help you.</p> 
          <p>Happy day for everyone. ?</p>

          <span class="name">Szymon Stasik <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127345"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-24T08:04:21+00:00">March 24, 2016 at 8:04 am</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>After reading various argument the main conclusion for me is that while it is good to not reinvent the wheel and have ability to use even simple helper functions then on the other hand it is insane to have separate module for any single (or even couple) line of code.<br> Looking not that far on somehow more mature OS development environment – there are also common libraries, like i.e. glibc, however they are aggregating many various common things. Now I wonder why this is has not happen in the javascript/node/npm to develop similar common core package(s)?</p>

          <img alt="" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/8974424ab9a0e4e4e84a6c3b2ce8db3f?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/8974424ab9a0e4e4e84a6c3b2ce8db3f?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">

         <div id="comment-127346" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name">Rob <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127346"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-24T08:04:51+00:00">March 24, 2016 at 8:04 am</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>Unequivocably yes! It’s why I always get downvoted into oblivion on amateur sites like Reddit where any mere mention of learning how to code instead of piecing together other people’s code is scoffed at and made fun of while making funny sentences out of random words using javascript is front page news. </p> 
          <p>Among today’s programmer’s, far too many are trained by scouring the web and composed of people who find making programs (more often games) exciting and not a thought process. Those who want to do it right are made fun of with “don’t reinvent the wheel” or “why do it the hard way when you can just use a package?” type thinking. </p> 
          <p>Such people never learn how computers really work and, typically, trail behind adapting new technology if they are in the industry at all three years later.</p>

       <li class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="li-comment-127355"> <a name="comment-127355"></a> 
        <div class="comment-container"> 
         <div class="avatar">
          <img alt="" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/17db559f7dc4475f34cabe7bf3552609?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/17db559f7dc4475f34cabe7bf3552609?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
         </div> 
         <div id="comment-127355" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name">Kyle <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127355"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-24T09:26:03+00:00">March 24, 2016 at 9:26 am</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>LeftPad is a **package**? Yikes.</p> 
          <p>I have many thoughts on this, but its been a few years since I’ve done serious JavaScript, so my observations may be complete bunk.</p> 
          <p>Let’s not assume everyone’s stupid.</p> 
          <p>This is a symptom of a deeper problem. </p> 
          <p>Cause 1: JavaScript has a feature-poor core library, and doesn’t include standard functions LeftPad.</p> 
          <p>Cause 2: There is a lack of cohesion in the JavaScript community because of constant library churn. So there is no longer even a de facto standard library (sort of like the position jQuery occupied for years). If there were such a de facto standard package, LeftPad would get added to it.</p> 
          <p>Cause 3: Javascript now appears to have a decent package system that makes it easy to install and use lightweight dependencies (I haven’t used javascript for a few years, so this is my impression).</p> 
          <p>Cause 4: Who wants to gives the honest but foolish standup the next morning: “Among other things, I wrote LeftPad yesterday”. There’s at least one evil bastard on every sizable team. If you’re good enough to write LeftPad without thinking, you’re probably also more talented than the evil bastard. This makes the evil bastard itchy to find something to pin on you. You just gave the evil bastard a foothold… “You are not focused on the big picture”… “You are reinventing the wheel”… “Why are you not using the LeftPad package? It’s on NPM.”</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127355#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127355&quot;, &quot;127355&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Kyle">Reply</a> 
          </div>

          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127366"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-24T10:24:17+00:00">March 24, 2016 at 10:24 am</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>These are all fixable problems. Heuristics and analysis could detect these rancid packages if it the need arises. While for most part, the crowds have more wisdom in selecting value and nurturing projects in the open source community, a few outliers will need addition policing. </p> 
          <p>The paradox of choice takes an order of magnitude to extreme when the number of packages and open source forks reaches these numbers. So curation and leadership remain important helping developers be successful in their decisions.</p> 
          <p>I think the question about have we forgotten how to code is the one we keep asking ourselves every year for decades. I recall seeing an early assignment in jr. high school writing different sorting algorithms in BASIC, and thought to myself, hasn’t someone else already written this subroutine? Does every programmer need to write their own quicksort? Yes, and No.</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127366#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127366&quot;, &quot;127366&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Ben L">Reply</a> 
          </div>
          <!-- /.reply --> 
         </div>
         <!-- /comment-content --> 
         <div class="fix"></div> 
        </div>

       <li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1" id="li-comment-127371"> <a name="comment-127371"></a> 
        <div class="comment-container"> 
         <div class="avatar">
          <img alt="" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/510afab91baab843c902796732fd0518?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/510afab91baab843c902796732fd0518?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
         </div> 
         <div id="comment-127371" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name"><a href="http://ejjohnson.net" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Erick J</a> <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127371"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-24T10:47:28+00:00">March 24, 2016 at 10:47 am</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>How is this surprising?</p> 
          <p>The unfortunate state of things is that much of the node/npm community are a hangover of script kiddies from the JQuery and Rails cargo cults. Much of this same community can be found on stackoverflow and hackernews reinforcing each others bad ideas. Those arguing that dynamic/meta/duck-type/flavor-of-the-week programming isn’t scalable get voted down as being unhip or uncool or unknowing.</p> 
          <p>8 years ago the cults worshiped Rails and Prototype/Scriptaculous with ERB templates (because writing your JS in Ruby was obviously the best). Then they used HAML and jQuery.UI. Then handlebars, but if you were really cool it was mustache (or the other way around?). Then the server thinned out and batmanJS sproutcore’d a backbone. Then someone lit an ember under angular. $ lost to _ and lodash, a bazillion other microframeworks. “Hey do you call .toString()” ever? Well use this toString-npm”. Then came the age of erlang/haskell/rust/Go because you have to design your tiny website from the ground up monadically processing your process trees for 1e9 QPS, just in case. Now we’re in the midst of React and Nodejs, because why wouldn’t you want to write in JSX and be limited to 1 core. Some of these trends last longer than others. Most turn out to be terrible</p> 
          <p>I will continue to happily ignore 99% of these trends, sticking to more established practices.</p> 
          <p>The question isn’t “Have We Forgotten How To Program?” it’s “Did we ever learn?”</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127371#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127371&quot;, &quot;127371&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Erick J">Reply</a> 
          </div>

       <li class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="li-comment-127385"> <a name="comment-127385"></a> 
        <div class="comment-container"> 
         <div class="avatar">
          <img alt="" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/3c7f633dec1fbacbb0cd2119b4ae5d84?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/3c7f633dec1fbacbb0cd2119b4ae5d84?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
         </div> 
         <div id="comment-127385" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name">Nanang Mahdaen El Agung <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127385"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-24T12:11:37+00:00">March 24, 2016 at 12:11 pm</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>I think depend on what we need. The `isArray()` package (for example) is something I (or we) use everyday on every projects. So better to load the existing one than re-writing for each projects. But, if we only need `isArray()` and we load Angular to get `angular.isArray()`, this is would be totally wrong since better to spend less than 5 minutes (I believe it should be less than 2 min) to write that code.</p> 
          <p>But, we (developers) should try to understand our languages before deciding to choose which libraries we’ll use. For example, if peoples working on javascript projects and they load `isArray()` module, then probably they don’t know javascript, since javascript has built-in `Array.isArray()` (except if they work on very old javascript :D).</p> 
          <p>So why micro modules exist? Because its help developers to get the daily use functions that do not exist yet. Like the `left-pad` module, if we have 10 projects that require that function, why we need to waste time to write it 10 times? It’s not (always) because we’ve forgotten how to program, but sometimes our boss say “You must complete it in 1 hour!”. But if we load Angular to get `angular.isArray()` while built-in `Array.isArray()` exist, then maybe we don’t know how to program.</p> 
          <p>Cheers!</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127385#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127385&quot;, &quot;127385&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Nanang Mahdaen El Agung">Reply</a> 
          </div>

         <li class="comment odd alt depth-2" id="li-comment-127436"> <a name="comment-127436"></a> 
          <div class="comment-container"> 
           <div class="avatar">
            <img alt="" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/f0306d02fb4dd40c46e665f03f9a1558?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/f0306d02fb4dd40c46e665f03f9a1558?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
           </div> 
           <div id="comment-127436" class="comment-content"> 
            <span class="name">PA1 <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
            <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127436"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-24T19:56:25+00:00">March 24, 2016 at 7:56 pm</time></a> </span> 
            <span class="edit"></span> 
            <p>There appears to be a preference to use a Package rather than a native capability of JS. I do not understand why.</p> 
            <p>MDN Array.isArray with pollyfill for &lt; IE9.</p> 
            <p><a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Array/isArray" rel="nofollow">https://developer.mozilla.org/en/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Array/isArray</a></p> 
            <div class="reply"> 
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127436#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127436&quot;, &quot;127436&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to PA1">Reply</a>

        <div class="comment-container"> 
         <div class="avatar">

         </div> 
         <div id="comment-127417" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name">Nerot <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127417"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-24T16:54:53+00:00">March 24, 2016 at 4:54 pm</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>Everyone leaping to NPM’s defense with arguments like ‘a bunch of dependencies is better than every developer re-writing some code every time’ is missing the point. Get back to the discussion of whether it’s better to inline your own code or import someone else’s, after sorting out the obviously, painfully clear issue that a house made of dependencies IS going to fail. Sometime, someday, it will.</p> 
          <p>And guess what? it did.</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127417#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127417&quot;, &quot;127417&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Nerot">Reply</a>

        <ul class="children"> 
         <li class="comment even depth-2" id="li-comment-127429"> <a name="comment-127429"></a> 
          <div class="comment-container"> 
           <div class="avatar">
            <img alt="" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/6eb701e5f5cc7b7754750ed4d22b9b75?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/6eb701e5f5cc7b7754750ed4d22b9b75?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
           </div> 
           <div id="comment-127429" class="comment-content"> 
            <span class="name"><a href="http://Service-governance.org" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Peter Brooks</a> <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
            <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127429"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-24T19:03:25+00:00">March 24, 2016 at 7:03 pm</time></a> </span> 
            <span class="edit"></span> 
            <p>Microcode, that’s where you really can program. Can you shorten those five lines of code to three, by adding pre-fetches in the rightmost two bytes so they can be snapped out of the pipeline in the third instruction? </p> 
            <p>It gives a great feeling of control to be able to do so much in what is, to the untutored eye, one assemble language instruction. </p> 
            <p>I was lucky to have the job of teaching some BT engineers to microprogram – the HP A900 had a very elegant micro architecture, and, best of all, you wrote the microcode in a high-level pascal-like language, you could pack multiple micro instructions into one word by the simple expedient of leaving out semicolons:</p> 
            <p>a = b + c;<br> If a &gt; d then do x;</p> 
            <p>Gives you two words </p> 
            <p>a = b + c<br> If a &gt; d then do x;</p> 
            <p>Puts them both into one word. </p> 
            <p>Of course, the second might not work, unless you’d prefetched the ‘d’ earlier.</p> 
            <p>Oh, and the beauty of it – at the same time you could have some floating point arithmetic going on – the FPL took three cycles to complete, so, if you were cunning, you could interleave tons of useful logic, instead of just waiting.</p> 
            <p>The HP1000 had a sixteen bit word, but the micro machine had a twenty four bit word – plenty of space to express yourself. </p> 
            <p>I really, really, must have enjoyed this at the time, to remember all this stuff 30 odd years later!</p> 
            <div class="reply"> 
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127429#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127429&quot;, &quot;127429&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Peter Brooks">Reply</a> 
            </div>
            <!-- /.reply --> 
           </div>

       <li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1" id="li-comment-127437"> <a name="comment-127437"></a> 
        <div class="comment-container"> 
         <div class="avatar">
          <img alt="" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/88a8ac71f1d3f24ed5253d3ca9fc018f?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/88a8ac71f1d3f24ed5253d3ca9fc018f?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
         </div> 
         <div id="comment-127437" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name">Scorpions4ever <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127437"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-24T20:21:54+00:00">March 24, 2016 at 8:21 pm</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>Was surprised that no one has yet commented that the original code is inefficient and has a couple of lurking bugs as well.<br> 1. There aren’t checks to see if str is undefined, null, Object, boolean etc. Ideally, it should only pad arguments of type string or number<br> 2. Why loop n times and construct multiple temporary string objects, when you can just use return ch.repeat(len – str.length) + str. Instead of constructing a bunch of temporary javascript strings in the loop and assignging it each time, the .repeat() call makes a single JS call to the interpreter to construct the string (which presumably calls much faster C code to construct the string) and then does one string append.</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127437#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127437&quot;, &quot;127437&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Scorpions4ever">Reply</a> 
          </div>
          <!-- /.reply --> 
         </div>
         <!-- /comment-content --> 
         <div class="fix"></div> 
        </div>
        <!-- /.comment-container --> 
        <div class="fix"></div> 
        <ul class="children"> 
         <li class="comment even depth-2" id="li-comment-127458"> <a name="comment-127458"></a> 
          <div class="comment-container"> 
           <div class="avatar">
            <img alt="" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/15f111b4e413a12de6dd05745e674199?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/15f111b4e413a12de6dd05745e674199?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
           </div> 
           <div id="comment-127458" class="comment-content"> 
            <span class="name">Anonymous Coder <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
            <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127458"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-25T03:22:04+00:00">March 25, 2016 at 3:22 am</time></a> </span> 
            <span class="edit"></span> 
            <p>String.prototype.repeat() is new as of ES6. Meaning that it has only been around since last year.</p> 
            <p>The more “normal” way to do something like that is Array.prototype.join(), which has been around since ES1 (1997).</p> 
            <div class="reply"> 
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127458#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127458&quot;, &quot;127458&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Anonymous Coder">Reply</a>

        <div class="comment-container"> 
         <div class="avatar">
          <img alt="" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/6811db2b37e824fdf6c5c4fcdddd4146?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/6811db2b37e824fdf6c5c4fcdddd4146?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
         </div> 
         <div id="comment-127439" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name"><a href="http://articles.runtings.co.uk/" rel="external nofollow" class="url">rtpHarry</a> <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127439"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-24T20:39:08+00:00">March 24, 2016 at 8:39 pm</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>People who are saying no to using these micro dependencies and saying we should write it all ourselves, I get it, when I first started I insisted on doing the Int13h programming myself instead of relying on Allegro. I wanted to write it all myself and do it properly.</p> 
          <p>I hit lots of walls, and then when I started doing it professionally I didn’t have that luxury to solve each problem myself and take an hour to deeply understand the issue. I needed to get it done within a quote that my clients would accept.</p> 
          <p>These days writing it all myself is even less of an attractive prospect because there are little glitches out there and more devices than we can test against. We might think we have solved the problem but maybe on platform X this gotcha appears and then our users get bad stuff all up in there faces.</p> 
          <p>Its being touted as “left-pad broke the internet”. </p> 
          <p>In reality millions and millions of npm packages are used all the time without problems. What actually happened was a couple of big packages has a couple of hours of mild disruption. It was a rare case occurrence.</p> 
          <p>The XKCD I kept expecting to get referenced for this argument (debate) is <a href="https://xkcd.com/378/" rel="nofollow">https://xkcd.com/378/</a></p> 
          <p>This is one of those debates that will never be settled because both sides are right for a given scenario.</p>

           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127439#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127439&quot;, &quot;127439&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to rtpHarry">Reply</a>

       <li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="li-comment-127465"> <a name="comment-127465"></a> 
        <div class="comment-container"> 
         <div class="avatar">
          <img alt="" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/56becfd433036d9599d8eadc480fe21e?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/56becfd433036d9599d8eadc480fe21e?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
         </div> 
         <div id="comment-127465" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name"><a href="http://leftyftw.wordpress.com" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Jaime Torres</a> <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127465"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-25T08:34:26+00:00">March 25, 2016 at 8:34 am</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>What seems to be forgotten is when shimming JavaScript, it’s a lot like adding a C# extension in System package. Because you’re adding it to base-object prototypes, the ENTIRE application gets it, not just your namespace. So if I pull in angular, and bootstrap, and underscore, and my own package, and each of those needs a “leftpad” solution, and they followed this articles advice: there would now be four flavors of leftpad sitting on String.prototype. If each were 11 lines long, I now have 44 lines dedicated to left-padding a string. By importing a microlibrary, there is but one, and 11 lines of code. At this point, who forgot to program? The guy that doesn’t know how to leverage the works of others and build an application, or the guy who wants to reinvent the wheel that’s already been built four times in his application?</p> 
          <p>Pragmatic developers aren’t stupid, they’re efficient.</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127465#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127465&quot;, &quot;127465&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Jaime Torres">Reply</a> 
          </div>

         </div>

       <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" id="li-comment-127470"> <a name="comment-127470"></a> 
        <div class="comment-container"> 
         <div class="avatar">
          <img alt="" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/fd65bf3cee92a016c186ffa1e7b692e6?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/fd65bf3cee92a016c186ffa1e7b692e6?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
         </div> 
         <div id="comment-127470" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name">Laurent Hasson <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127470"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-25T11:32:02+00:00">March 25, 2016 at 11:32 am</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>We went from spaghetti code to spaghetti component dependencies. Computing “constructs” have an optimal size. I strongly believe that. One-line functions always bothered me, even with compiler inlining capabilities. Interfaces with one method, classes with one method etc… There has got to be a way to think about these things as an ROI system for example.</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127470#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127470&quot;, &quot;127470&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Laurent Hasson">Reply</a>

       <li class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="li-comment-127489"> <a name="comment-127489"></a> 
        <div class="comment-container"> 
         <div class="avatar">
          <img alt="" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/c53bff5fc583ccc237a55b3930ae3271?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/c53bff5fc583ccc237a55b3930ae3271?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
         </div> 
         <div id="comment-127489" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name">Orv <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127489"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-26T00:16:49+00:00">March 26, 2016 at 12:16 am</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>Several years back, a major security hole was discovered in the zlib compression code. Now, for the reasons the author notes, a lot of projects over the years had simply cut-and-pasted the zlib code. That made things nice and simple…until suddenly it was urgent to fix problems with that code. Now dozens of projects had to fix their own private zlib implementations, and I had to track down updates for them, instead of simply updating a shared zlib library and being done with it.</p> 
          <p>When you make your own copy of an implementation, you’re basically forking it. You have to maintain it, keep track of security issues, etc. It’s a non-trivial amount of ongoing maintenance.</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127489#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127489&quot;, &quot;127489&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Orv">Reply</a>

       <li class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="li-comment-127677"> <a name="comment-127677"></a> 
        <div class="comment-container"> 
         <div class="avatar">
          <img alt="" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/f35b255fdf372e406c6b9bb3a1d13420?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/f35b255fdf372e406c6b9bb3a1d13420?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
         </div> 
         <div id="comment-127677" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name">Yuriy <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-127677"><time pubdate datetime="2016-03-30T16:13:39+00:00">March 30, 2016 at 4:13 pm</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>Actually, I totally agree with you with one minor difference:</p> 
          <p>It’s not that JS developers forgot how to program, it’s because majority of JS developers didn’t know how to program.</p> 
          <p>Let me elaborate on why IMO majority of JS developers didn’t know how to program:<br> 1. JS from the start as a language was meant for very low-level developers with very low entry level. For most of JS developers it is and was first language to start from and for many of them it’s the only language they know. That’s why no matter how proficient JS developer is (and there are very proficient ones), they were and are forced to produce libraries that even very low level developers would understand and could use, even if this library doesn’t follow common modularisation principles or separation of concerns.</p> 
          <p> 2. JS was never meant for modularisation – it was created to be included / injected into HTML with global scope variables without any namespaces / packages / modules. And the reason for this was item 1 above – because if there are namespaces / packages / modules, it would complicate language and prevent entry level developers to use JS. So JS from the start was contradicting basic property of structured programming languages – modularity. This was overcome with packing things into local variables inside objects which served and serve as modules, however whole JS community started using it in approx. 2006 i.e. 10 years after initial JS release which again proves item 1.</p> 
          <p>That’s why whole JS community does what’s more simpler in the first place and usually doesn’t care if it’s right or not. And even prosperous JS developers couldn’t resist that and try to “moderate” whole community to use right libraries and right modularisation principles. That’s why I would say that JS is doomed to some extent because it has no entry level requirements to be used.</p> 
          <p>Personally I wrote algorithms like leftpad in 9th grade in flowcharts and in Pascal as a homework and I clearly understood that this is not something to be released for general public by me, because such libraries existed in Pascal for years written by more experienced developers during the first years when Pascal came out. Then I switched to C++ and found out that 99% of needed functions are already present in libraries like STD, written and tested long ago by more experienced developers. So while I was implementing sorting algorithms on lists by myself as a homework and practice, I would never ever thought of releasing it to public.</p> 
          <p>The fact that such libraries are released and used by the public confirms once again that JS community is still very immature in it’s majority and is by no means suited for writing big applications.</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=127677#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-127677&quot;, &quot;127677&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Yuriy">Reply</a> 
          </div>

          <span class="name">Eric S <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-128028"><time pubdate datetime="2016-04-15T12:10:39+00:00">April 15, 2016 at 12:10 pm</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>The underlying problem is that programmers do no know how to program, but that most programmers do not understand complexity very well, and are not good at evaluating whether a solution adds more complexity than the problem is solves.</p>

       <li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1" id="li-comment-128127"> <a name="comment-128127"></a> 
        <div class="comment-container"> 
         <div class="avatar">
          <img alt="" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/378abc2782d597e5e5ed3388a7e1813b?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/378abc2782d597e5e5ed3388a7e1813b?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
         </div> 
         <div id="comment-128127" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name">MGH <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-128127"><time pubdate datetime="2016-04-20T17:40:58+00:00">April 20, 2016 at 5:40 pm</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>I’m interested in the 250+ comments (using the post before this one rather than determining it for myself) where only the last has mentioned documentation of modules. I may be old-school, but I’m used to APIs that actually tell you what you need to know to use the API. I don’t have much knowledge of modules and none of npm, but my experience so far is that module documentation usually consists of little more than “here is my module that I wrote, use it and it will save you lots of time!” But then I have to spend time figuring out how to use it, what happens in edge cases, whether it is better than the oodles of other modules that do the same thing, most of which involves reading the code. I spend more effort solving what happens when things don’t go as expected than when they do, and this is very difficult when I don’t know what the module I’m using does. I guess most developers are only interested in making things work most of the time, programming using examples and trial-and-error, which is probably why most software these days is so poor.</p> 
          <p>The other thing I’m surprised about is that nobody has mentioned “JavaScript – The Definitive Guide” that tells you everything you need to know about the language. Or that JavaScript is a powerful, but misunderstood, language with prototypal inheritance. It is no wonder that many developers “do not know how to program” in JS.</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=128127#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-128127&quot;, &quot;128127&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to MGH">Reply</a>

          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-130779"><time pubdate datetime="2016-10-05T08:36:37+00:00">October 5, 2016 at 8:36 am</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>About your question in the heading, not everyone has forgotten how to program, the trouble is elsewhere. Young programmers are forced to accomplish task easily with minimum of own code present. A junior I taught to program has become kind of assembler. The goal is to find everything you need as an dependency and assemble it together. </p> 
          <p>You don’t here in the company: too big overhead! whole package for simple function? are you crazy?<br> Right now: don’t reinvent the wheel, assemble the parts together, we have sufficient bandwidth and space. </p> 
          <p>And the domino effect, it’s dependency of another library; I will use it too. It’s there anyway, and it will remain there, even after the dependency in question is no longer necessary.</p> 
          <p>It’s all about money, producing nice and tiny code is no longer the target. Most of your colleagues don’t anayway and would not appreciate it. They’re no longer programmers…</p>
