          <span class="name">joe <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-131023"><time pubdate datetime="2016-10-19T10:11:36+00:00">October 19, 2016 at 10:11 am</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>if you have a myriad of micro packages the developer needs a larger vocabulary of package names. this is why namespacing took over in the Microsoft world, java, php etc. </p> 
          <p>trig.sin<br> trig.cos<br> trig.tan</p> 
          <p>requires you to remember trig only. once at trig, you follow your nose.</p> 
          <p>the low average age of the npm world blinds it to the long term maintenance debt being built up.</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=131023#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-131023&quot;, &quot;131023&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to joe">Reply</a> 
          </div>

          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>If you ask a modern JS dev to code a hello world program they’ll go npm install hello-world </p> 
          <p>There’s something wrong about that :p</p> 
          <div class="reply">

         <li class="comment even depth-2" id="li-comment-134604"> <a name="comment-134604"></a> 
          <div class="comment-container"> 
           <div class="avatar">
            <img alt="" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/cc440e737b604fd4abd9cb003494cb40?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/cc440e737b604fd4abd9cb003494cb40?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
           </div> 
           <div id="comment-134604" class="comment-content"> 
            <span class="name">Shaday Malloc <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
            <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-134604"><time pubdate datetime="2017-04-26T15:53:24+00:00">April 26, 2017 at 3:53 pm</time></a> </span> 
            <span class="edit"></span> 
            <p>Yes, and here is an analogy:</p> 
            <p>Using hundreds of small dependencies, instead of coding something yourself, is just like using TurboTax to file your tax returns. You can focus on what matters (deductions, earnings, car purchases, etc) and TurboTax can take care of putting that information into the proper forms.</p> 
            <p>However, you don’t claim to be an accountant. Imagine for a second that every accountant and tax attorney simply filed your taxes for you… but used TurboTax. You would say… “well, I could do that!” and you would be right.</p> 
            <p>This is the real problem. Programmers are using TurboTax to build software, and they don’t even interact with the tax forms (raw code), but instead are coding at a level where they no longer have control of the application if something actually goes wrong.</p> 
            <p>Programmers need to be programmers, and stop being lazy. They need to understand exactly what every inch of their program is doing so they can debug it properly.</p> 
            <div class="reply"> 
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=134604#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-134604&quot;, &quot;134604&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Shaday Malloc">Reply</a>

       <li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="li-comment-134398"> <a name="comment-134398"></a> 
        <div class="comment-container"> 
         <div class="avatar">
          <img alt="" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/b9b89d2ebb4ad79a3f0d622c96432b35?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/b9b89d2ebb4ad79a3f0d622c96432b35?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
         </div> 
         <div id="comment-134398" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name">David Fallah <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-134398"><time pubdate datetime="2017-04-12T15:23:20+00:00">April 12, 2017 at 3:23 pm</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>Seriously? I have to disagree with pretty much everything you’ve written here.</p> 
          <p>&gt; What concerns me here is that so many packages and projects took on a dependency for a simple left padding string function, rather than their developers taking 2 minutes to write such a basic function themselves.</p> 
          <p>What you’re asking is for people to reinvent wheels, which is generally acknowledged as a dumb thing to do.</p> 
          <p>Would you seriously rather have 10,000 people create their own “left pad” function, all of varying qualities and largely duplicating each other’s logic? Or would you prefer to have that logic consolidated into one package, which multiple people can contribute to to make it the best “left pad” function possible?</p> 
          <p>You’re advocating for people to write their own functions but all this does is bloat up their codebase with utility functions that have been created hundreds of times before.</p> 
          <p>&gt; There’s absolutely no guarantee that what someone else has written is correct, or even works well. </p> 
          <p>If someone has created a package that has high ratings/download counts, full access to the source code and clear evidence of testing, I can rest assured that their implementation is at the least sufficient for my needs and probably a lot better than anything I would implement myself.</p> 
          <p>&gt; Every package that you use adds yet another dependency to your project. Dependencies, by their very name, are things you need in order for your code to function. The more dependencies you take on, the more points of failure you have.</p> 
          <p>The more wheels you reinvent yourself, the more points of failure too. Except that at least when you download a package there’s a good chance other people have spotted and resolved flaws in it, which is not the case with your own newly-created and potentially buggy code.</p> 
          <p>&gt; Rather than write any functions or code, it seems that they prefer to depend on something that someone else has written. It feels to me as if the entire job of an NPM-participating developer is writing the smallest amount of code possible to string existing library calls together in order to create something new that functions uniquely for their personal or business need.</p> 
          <p>Which is exactly as I feel it should be. Reuse the work other people have done so you’re not wasting time, effort and money doing it yourself. Write the minimal amount of unique code necessary to adapt these libraries to your own use case. This is so incredibly basic…</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=134398#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-134398&quot;, &quot;134398&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to David Fallah">Reply</a> 
          </div>

       <li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1" id="li-comment-135683"> <a name="comment-135683"></a> 
        <div class="comment-container"> 
         <div class="avatar">
          <img alt="" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/025df90894af55a0d6bf69549577f5df?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/025df90894af55a0d6bf69549577f5df?s=160&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-80 photo" height="80" width="80">
         </div> 
         <div id="comment-135683" class="comment-content"> 
          <span class="name">Toumal <span class="says">says :</span></span> 
          <span class="date"> <a href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/#comment-135683"><time pubdate datetime="2017-07-04T12:08:03+00:00">July 4, 2017 at 12:08 pm</time></a> </span> 
          <span class="edit"></span> 
          <p>I’m amazed and bewildered at some of the comments here attacking the author and defending silly things such as a library that *adds spaces to a string*.</p> 
          <p>“It’s about hiding complexity”<br> “It’s about not reinventing the wheel”</p> 
          <p>Seriously? I really hope the people who think that way do not work in any capacity where their output is used in any sort of safety critical application.<br> If you do not know the difference between a library and a function, if you think lpad is “hiding complexity” then please seek a different occupation. </p> 
          <p>Handling http or even the intricacies of file paths on various platforms is certainly a different matter, depending on the library of course. There is something to be said for a library for core functionality, just think apache commons. Using such a library comes with its own benefits and drawbacks (which the author here acknowledged).</p> 
          <p>But for padding a string? There should not even be a *debate* about this. But here we are, and people in the JS world “invent” stuff that’s been done to death before and well understood, without learning from the mistakes of others. There’s a reason why you can’t un-publish something from maven for example. The npm guys learned this the hard way.</p> 
          <p>So yeah. If you think lpad is a good library to have and use, please seek education. It’s okay, we’ve all been there. I once thought it’s a great idea to write my own XML parser… using substring in Java, when there was plenty of excellent alternatives. I’ve been an idiot. I should’ve used XPP or XStream or even SAX or DOM parsers.</p> 
          <p>lpad is just as wrong. The thing is: I suffered for my own stupid mistakes. Sadly I see more and more devs even in my company who just pass on their stuff to maintenance and they never get to feel the consequences of their incompetence.</p> 
          <p>I can see the first man on mars being killed on landing because some guy hasn’t “invented” priority scheduling yet.</p> 
          <div class="reply"> 
           <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="http://www.haneycodes.net/npm-left-pad-have-we-forgotten-how-to-program/?replytocom=135683#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-135683&quot;, &quot;135683&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;824&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Toumal">Reply</a> 
          </div>
